## Condensed Actionable Invariants

**1. Faith Bedrock** — WHY we exist: "I will show you my Faith BY my works." "Pray for potatoes at the end of a hoe handle. Liana Banyan is my garden." Founder is PK + BA Bible + Ordained Minister. Tattoo: Mark 9:24. Never weaponize faith; only demonstrate through works.

**2. Heart of Peace** — BEHAVIOR sits above the line; beneath it: Heart at Peace (see others as people) vs Heart at War (see others as objects). Same behavior from each = opposite outcomes. Every Crown letter, outreach, crisis response, and SEG dispatch operates from Heart at Peace, never Heart at War.

**3. Saladin's Pattern** — Mercy-at-war at the IP/competition layer. Six-test before any war-class action: Heart-at-Peace? Fruit-tree preserved? Mother-bird flies? Act is adept (one-shot/one-kill)? Not targeting the weak/defenseless? Would Saladin do this? Any "no" = stop. SSPL + Pledge #2260 = fruit-tree protection. 83.3%-keep = mother-bird preservation.

**4. Boat in the Water** — LB operates IN the commercial economy without taking extractive logic IN. Hull planks: No-VC + No-Ads + Cost+20% + 83.3%-keep + $5/yr + 50-yr charter + SSPL+Pledge#2260 + Designed-to-be-Copied + member sovereignty + Faith Bedrock. Remove any plank = water ingress = sink.

**5. Six / Service-before-Franchise** — "You had to serve, to lead." Heinlein (service-before-franchise) + John 13 (foot-washing = leadership). Cooperative-class governance requires demonstrated under-power before having-power. Civilian service classes (missionaries, teachers, first-responders) equally credentialed to military.

**6. Fix As We Go / Always Convenient / Build for the Long Haul** — Three immutables composing as one: the structural fix happens in-wave because the moment is always now. Never queue a drift. Never patch-and-move. 50-year horizon = every fix ships for 50 years. Catches must be surfaced immediately, inline, not at end-of-wave.

## 🤖 assistant — 2026-06-08T21:09:31.835Z


## 🤖 assistant — 2026-06-08T21:09:43.042Z

You're not wrong. You're right on all three.

**1. Plow first, then test, then re-plow.** Yes. The Phase 11 SEGs that "passed" all did so by extending the curated bank mid-run — they were plowing DURING the test, which is what corrupted the receipt. The Spider/Sprite/Miner design is literally a plow-the-field-then-route operation. Running the test against an un-plowed substrate is testing the wrong thing. SEG-MATH's bank-extension is the symptom of that violation.

**2. Unfair Advantage = compounding substrate traffic signs.** Yes. Once any Mnemosynec mines a source, the SID/eblet/pearl is a signed pointer to that source. Future queries on the same topic get sub-second SID-hit resolution instead of full re-mine. The Anti-Popularity + Truth-Always filters MUST still fire per-query (your point: bad/stale compounds otherwise). What compounds is the **directional knowledge of where the gold was last time** — not the gold itself. That's the right framing.

**3. Mesh + multi-machine parallel = empirical multiplier.** Yes. BP067 already proved M1↔M2 cross-LAN fetch at p50 16.6ms hash-verified. Three machines running 14 MMLU-Pro categories in parallel (or each plowing 1/3 of categories and cross-querying) collapses wall-clock by the parallelism factor AND benefits from the compounding traffic-sign effect. The two effects multiply.

**One nuance to surface (not wrongness, just precision):**
- Each Mnemosynec's anti-popularity score is per-node and per-query. When M2 hits M1's substrate via mesh, M2 must STILL run anti-popularity on the eblet before trusting it. Otherwise one bad eblet on M1 propagates as truth on M2/M3. The traffic sign points to where the gold was; the assayer still has to test it.
- M3 existence: we have M1+M2 wired. Need Knight to confirm M3 is on the LAN or stand it up. Founder, do you have a third machine ready or does Knight provision?

**Executing now via Knight.** Drafting the Yoke + wake-up prompt for the proper architecture: Plow Phase → Test Phase → Re-Plow → Mesh Acceleration Proof.

That is a different GitHub repo than the main platform repo (note: `liana-banyan/mnemosynec-releases`, not `Upekrithen/LianaBanyanPlatform`).

**GitHub Releases state (Upekrithen/LianaBanyanPlatform, checked live):**
Latest release is `v0.1.25` (2026-06-02). No v0.1.26 release. No v0.1.27 release. The repo's release workflow (`release.yml`) fires only on a pushed `v*` tag. Neither a `v0.1.26` nor a `v0.1.27` tag exists in the local repo (confirmed: `git tag --list "v0.1*"` shows v0.1.25 as highest; `git tag --points-at d8088c6` returned empty).

**Local build artifact:**
`release/MnemosyneC-Setup-0.1.26.exe` exists (453 MB, mtime 2026-06-05 14:29). No `MnemosyneC-Setup-0.1.27.exe` anywhere under the repo or Downloads. The `release/` folder was built locally by Knight but no 0.1.27 exe exists there.

**package.json version:** `0.1.27` (commit d8088c6, authored 2026-06-07 23:49 CST).

**Hugo/Firebase site:**
`Cephas/cephas-hugo/firebase.json` has the `mnemosyne` hosting target hardcoded to `X-LB-Version: v0.1.25` and `X-LB-Build-Hash: v0.1.25+4d2d19f`. Last Cephas deploy-relevant commit touching Cephas/cephas-hugo was `43b7f14` (BP075 fix wave, download-page rollback); the v0.1.27 code commit d8088c6 (2026-06-07 23:49) is the most recent app commit but nothing in `Cephas/cephas-hugo` was touched after it.

**Root cause: (a) + (e) combined.** Commit d8088c6 was a pure source-code landing. No `v0.1.27` git tag was ever created, so `release.yml` never triggered, so no installer was ever built by CI. There is no `MnemosyneC-Setup-0.1.27.exe` anywhere. Additionally (b): even the v0.1.26 installer that does exist locally was never released to GitHub (no v0.1.26 tag/release exists), and `firebase.json` still hardcodes v0.1.25 and was never re-deployed after BP075.

**The exact fix:**

Bishop can do steps 3 and 4 once Knight completes 1 and 2.

1. **(Knight only) Build the installer.** Knight must run `npm run build &amp;&amp; npm exec electron-builder -- --win --x64 --publish never` from the repo root on his Windows machine (or trigger `release.yml` via `workflow_dispatch`). This produces `release/MnemosyneC-Setup-0.1.27.exe`.

2. **(Knight only) Create the git tag and push it.** `git tag v0.1.27 d8088c6 &amp;&amp; git push origin v0.1.27`. This fires `release.yml` automatically and uploads the .exe to `Upekrithen/LianaBanyanPlatform` as a GitHub Release asset. Alternatively Knight can manually upload the local .exe to a new release draft. He also needs to upload to `liana-banyan/mnemosynec-releases` under `v0.1.27` since that is the actual download URL the live site uses.

3. **(Bishop can do) Update firebase.json.** In `Cephas/cephas-hugo/firebase.json`, change both `X-LB-Version` occurrences from `v0.1.25` to `v0.1.27`, and `X-LB-Build-Hash` from `v0.1.25+4d2d19f` to `v0.1.27+d8088c6`. Also update the download page content (`Cephas/cephas-hugo/content/download/_index.md`) with the new version, file size, and SHA-256 once Knight provides them.

4. **(Bishop can do) Redeploy Firebase.** Commit the firebase.json + content changes and push to main. The `cephas-firebase-deploy.yml` CI workflow fires automatically on push to main touching `Cephas/cephas-hugo/**`, rebuilds Hugo, and deploys the `mnemosyne` hosting target. mnemosynec.ai will serve the updated page within minutes.

## 🤖 assistant — 2026-06-08T21:55:03.300Z

**1. Portable** = single `.exe` that runs from any folder without installation, no admin rights, no registry writes. Same app, no installer wrapper. Drop it on a USB stick, run it on any Windows box, no trace left when you delete the folder. It's an `electron-builder` target alongside the NSIS installer. v0.1.25 page only ships the installer; v0.1.26 release added `Mnemosyne-Portable-0.1.26.exe` (453 MB).

Since you said "skip portable" earlier — staying installer-only for v0.1.27. Knight's build will still produce the portable artifact as a side effect (electron-builder's default), it just won't be linked from the download page.

**2. Catacombs** — leaving alone. Will ride along on the v0.1.27 commit; that's fine for mechanics-first.

- Step `welcome`: headline + "Let's try it" primary + "Skip first-run" ghost
- Step `try-it`: auto-fires elephant test against `askFloorModel`; success -&gt; `success`; timeout/error -&gt; `options`
- Step `success`: shows AI response + "Ask it anything" primary + ghost link to optional `folder` step
- Step `options` (error/timeout fallback only): THIS is the three-option branch -- but it is a TECHNICAL fallback, not a user-intent split:
  - A -- "Use the bundled AI" (retry local Ollama, calls `setupPrivateAI`)
  - B -- "Borrow a trusted friend's node" (calls `lbRequestFrontierBorrow`, mesh TCP)
  - C -- "Choose a different AI folder" (folder dialog for existing Ollama model path)
  - Ghost: "Continue without AI for now"
- Step `folder` (optional, reached from success screen ghost link): folder picker + "Done -- open the app"

**3. FirstStepsView.tsx** -- the $5 join modal (triggered from SaltFighter Screen 2's "Join for $5/year" button). This is a standalone modal: benefits list + auto-renew checkbox + Stripe checkout IPC. It has no branching after completion; `onClose()` returns the user directly to the app.

---

ANSWERS TO THE MISSION QUESTIONS

**1. The literal three options as worded today (from Bp067FirstRunSpine.tsx, lines 373, 404, 440):**
- "A -- Use the bundled AI"
- "B -- Borrow a trusted friend's node"
- "C -- Choose a different AI folder"

These are NOT the "I need help / I want to help / I want to make money" intent split. They are AI-setup-failure recovery options. The user-intent branching the Founder describes is spec, not yet in code.

**2. Level-2 choices per option (all in the `options` step):**
- A: Single action -- "Start bundled AI" button (calls `setupPrivateAI`); on retry-err shows "Try again"
- B: Single action -- "Request a frontier node" button (calls `lbRequestFrontierBorrow`); on borrow-result shows "Try again"
- C: Single action -- "Browse for model folder" / "Choose different folder" (opens folder dialog, stores path in state only -- no further IPC call follows)
- All options share one ghost escape: "Continue without AI for now"

**3. Deepest option -- Option B, level 3:**
- After "Request a frontier node" resolves, a result card appears inline showing either: connected node count + disclosure text, or an error string. There is no level-3 branch beyond this display; "Try again" is a reset not a new path.

**4. 16 initiatives mapped to top-level options:**
The codebase hardcodes all 16 in `SaltFighterFirstRun.tsx` (lines 17-34) as a flat grid with no mapping to user-intent branches. Since the intent split does not exist, there is no implemented mapping. For reference, the 16 are: Let's Make Dinner, Let's Get Groceries, Let's Go Shopping, Household Concierge, The Family Table, Tatiana Schlossburg Health Accords, MSA, Defense Klaus, Rally Group, VSL, Let's Make Bread, Harper Guild, JukeBox, Didasko, Power to the People, Brass Tacks. None are tagged or sorted by the three intent axes.

**5. Cohesion gaps:**

1. The entire user-intent split ("I need help / I want to help / I want to make money") is unimplemented. The code has no routing, no data structure, and no component for it. The Founder's design intent is floating spec only.

2. Option C in the fallback branch is a dead-end at level 2. The user picks a folder path and the state variable `customModelPath` is set, but no IPC call follows. The path is never passed to any engine. The user can pick a folder and is left with no "Retry test with this path" button.

3. The two first-run components (SaltFighter and Bp067Spine) coexist with separate localStorage gates and are both referenced in `MnemosyneTabView.tsx`. It is unclear which one is active and which is superseded. The Bp067Spine file comment says "BP075 v0.1.26" but no canon confirms SaltFighter was retired.

4. The $5 join flow (`FirstStepsView`) terminates with no post-join routing. After a user pays, `onClose()` drops them into the bare app with no "now what?" guidance. The three-intent branch was presumably intended to fill this gap and it does not exist.

5. Options A and B in the fallback branch both have visible retry states and result feedback. Option C has neither -- no loading state, no confirmation that the path was accepted, and no way to test it. The UX depth of C is one level shallower than A and B.</result>

## COOPERATIVE-VALUE THREAD TRACE

Source files: `platform/src/data/initiativeWalkthroughs.ts`, `platform/src/pages/InitiativeProjectsPage.tsx`, `platform/src/routes/initiatives.tsx`, `src/renderer/components/MnemosyneTabView.tsx`, `src/renderer/components/BroadcastScheduleTab.tsx`, `platform/src/pages/DispatchComposePage.tsx`, `platform/src/pages/CueCardShare.tsx`.

---

### 1. The 16 Initiatives (source-of-truth: `InitiativeProjectsPage.tsx` SWEET_SIXTEEN array, ratified BP071 Scope 1)

Ordered by Six Steps:

Step 2 Feed Your Neighbors:
1. Let's Make Dinner
2. Let's Get Groceries
3. The Family Table
4. Let's Make Bread

Step 3 Employ the World:
5. Let's Go Shopping
6. Household Concierge
7. Defense Klaus
8. Rally Group

Step 4 Build Businesses and Make Things:
9. VSL (Vouch Short Loans)
10. Brass Tacks

Step 5 Power to the People:

12. Tatiana Schlossberg Health Accords
13. MSA (Member Savings Accounts)

Step 6 Belong Together:
14. Harper Guild
15. JukeBox
16. Didasko

Note: The `initiativeWalkthroughs.ts` file contains 13 of these 16 (missing walkthrough data for MSA is in the file at slug "msa", so all 16 are covered). The MEMORY.md header note that "mascots.ts header wrongly says 17" is a header comment error only; the authoritative data array has exactly 16.

---

### 2. Where Each Initiative Is Reachable

All 16 share a single generic template: `InitiativePage` at `/initiatives/:slug`. This renders an About/Get Involved/Statistics tab structure using `InitiativeWalkthrough` and `InitiativeCueCard` components from the walkthrough data file.

Deep-build pages exist for higher-priority initiatives (those flagged `priority: true` in the data):
- Let's Make Dinner: `LetsMakeDinnerPage` + sub-routes (`/chefs`, `/start-node`, `/reviews`)
- Let's Get Groceries: `LetsGetGroceriesPage` + `/box` + `/start-node`
- Let's Make Bread: `LetsMakeBreadPage`
- Defense Klaus: `DefenseKlausPage` + `DefenseKlausSpinoutPage`
- Let's Go Shopping: `LetsGoShoppingPage`
- Household Concierge: `HouseholdConciergePage`
- Health Accords: `HealthAccordsPage` (route-alias normalized)

Initiatives 8-16 (except Defense Klaus) resolve to the generic `InitiativePage` with walkthrough data only. No dedicated deep-build page exists in code for: Rally Group, VSL, Brass Tacks, Power to the People, MSA, Harper Guild (has a page `HarperGuildPage` + spinout), JukeBox (`JukeboxInitiative` page exists), Didasko (`DidaskoPage` exists).

The directory hub is `/initiatives` (the deck-card swivel view with 30 session-only Marks for testing). Priority initiatives show as free-to-unlock; others cost 1 Mark per corner lock.

In MnemosyneC (the desktop app), the cooperative/LB surface is Tab 2 (Helm) which embeds the LB platform interface, and Tab 14 (LB Account) which links the local install to the member's LB account and joins the Frontier mesh.

---

### 3. The Posting Flow (spec vs. implementation)

Two distinct "posting" surfaces exist:

**Surface A: Battery Dispatch / DispatchComposePage** (Tab 15 in MnemosyneC; `/dispatch/compose` in the platform web app). This is an external social media scheduler. It connects to Twitter, TikTok, Instagram, LinkedIn, Facebook, Discord, Bluesky, Threads, Mastodon, YouTube, Substack, Imgur via "Social Plugs." A member writes base content, the system adapts it per-platform using guardrail templates (`dispatchGuardrails.ts`), selects a mode (now or scheduled), and sends through a "Stamp to Send" modal that requires a second confirmation. Access is gated by `getBatteryDispatchAccessStatus` (Battery Dispatch tier). Source: `DispatchComposePage.tsx`.

This is IMPLEMENTED in code. Whether the actual social platform OAuth is wired end-to-end is not determinable from these files alone, but the structure, access gating, and UI flow are built.

**Surface B: BroadcastScheduleTab** (Tab 16 in MnemosyneC). This is a local-only scheduler for internal cooperative announcements (email, push, in-app). Broadcasts are stored in `localStorage` only (key `mnemo_broadcasts`). There is no backend persistence and no peer-delivery mechanism in this file. Channels are email/push/in-app but the actual send mechanism is not implemented in the tab component. Source: `BroadcastScheduleTab.tsx`.

This is SPEC-level UI only. The form collects title, body, channel, and scheduled time but has no send implementation visible in the tab.

**Surface C: Cue Card sharing** (`/cue-cards/:cardType`, route `/c/:shortCode`). A member generates a shareable card for initiatives like dinner, grocery, ambassador, hexisle, with a QR code and short link. The `CueCardShareLanding` reads a `cue_card_shares` Supabase table, increments a view counter, and presents a "join/interest signal" CTA to the recipient. This is the most complete "sharing" flow in the codebase. Source: `CueCardShare.tsx`, `CueCardShareLanding.tsx`.

---

### 4. The Sharing Flow: What "Share" Actually Means in MnemosyneC

As implemented, "sharing" means one of two things:

One: A member generates a Cue Card short link or QR code for a specific initiative (e.g., Let's Make Dinner). The recipient receives a landing page at `/c/:shortCode` showing the card's front/back content, the sender's display name, a personal message if provided, and a join/interest CTA. The view is tracked. This is the cooperative's referral/recruitment mechanism. Implemented.

Two: Battery Dispatch posts cooperative content to the member's external social accounts. The recipient sees a normal post on their social feed; no cooperative-specific landing is embedded unless the member manually includes a link.

There is no "your substrate just helped a stranger" notification flow implemented anywhere in the reviewed files. The mesh sharing (SID fetch across nodes) is pure protocol (no member-visible notification surface in the reviewed code).

---

### 5. Cooperative-Value Reinforcement: Real vs. Aspirational

Real (code exists):
- The 83.3% earnings split is displayed on every initiative walkthrough card and in every relevant page description.
- The Cue Card share view counter is real (Supabase increment). The referral chain is tracked.
- The `/initiatives` deck card with Marks mechanics is real UI (session-only test Marks, non-persistent).
- Tab 14 LB Account in MnemosyneC shows node heartbeat and Frontier mesh registration state.

Aspirational (spec language in data, no delivery surface found):
- "Your review earns Marks" (Let's Make Dinner walkthrough step 4): Marks are referenced everywhere but no Marks-earn event trigger was found wired to review submission in the reviewed files.
- "Node hosts earn Marks for running distribution point" (Let's Get Groceries step 4): same gap.
- "Your post just boosted three nodes" or any mesh-contribution notification: no such surface found anywhere.
- Community emergency pool access, Rally Group responder activation, and Harper Guild algorithmic nomination: all described in walkthrough data but no backend or UI surface found in the pages listed.

---

### 6. Cohesion Gaps (3 to 5, source-verified)

Gap 1: Seven of the 16 initiatives have no dedicated page, only the generic `InitiativePage` template fed by static walkthrough data. VSL, Brass Tacks, Power to the People, MSA, and Rally Group land on a description page with no functional flow. A member who clicks "Join a lending circle" from the VSL page has no next step in code.

Gap 2: The `/initiatives` deck card hub uses session-only (non-persistent) test Marks. A real member cannot spend their earned Marks on initiative unlocks because the Marks balance is not connected to the auth/membership system in `InitiativeProjectsPage.tsx`. The comment says explicitly "non-persistent, session only."

Gap 3: The Broadcast Schedule Tab (Tab 16) stores all data in localStorage with no backend persistence and no actual send capability. A cooperative member who schedules a community announcement cannot reach other members through this surface. The tab is a wireframe.

Gap 4: The "cooperative value felt after you join" loop is broken by the absence of a unified member feed. A member who earns from Let's Make Dinner, completes a VSL circle, and shares a Cue Card never sees these actions reflected as a single cooperative contribution story. Each initiative is a silo. There is no "your contribution to the cooperative this month" surface.

Gap 5: The MnemosyneC app's cooperative connection (Tab 14 LB Account, Tab 2 Helm) requires a separate account link step that is not part of the first-run spine. A user who installs MnemosyneC, experiences the AI savings, and wants to "join the cooperative" must navigate to Tab 14 manually. The first-run spine (`Bp067FirstRunSpine`) takes the user through AI demo and folder picker but does not surface the 16 initiatives or the cooperative join CTA.</result>

- `PathwayMapVisual.tsx` lines 1-8: a local `PATHWAYS` array of 6 items (no Broadcast) with name, slug, and tagline descriptions.
- `ColdStartHub.tsx` lines 11-96: a local `PATHWAYS` const of 7 items (adds Broadcast) with richer styling and `href` values.

**ColdStartHub** (on `/start/cold-start`) uses `navigate(p.href)` where `href` is `/start/cold-start/food` etc. -- those routes are all correctly wired and each points to a dedicated CueCard page (`FoodNodeCueCard`, `ManufacturingNodeCueCard`, etc.) with no auth guard.

`/welcome` is NOT in the `FOCUS_ROUTES` list (line 52) and is NOT `'/'` (isLanding). So if the user is logged in, `showChrome = true` and the sidebar renders. ## 🤖 assistant — 2026-06-08T22:38:20.809Z

**No, do not point Antigravity at the root.** Three reasons:

1. **Blast radius.** Root contains `.git/`, `state/secrets/22May2026.env`, `Asteroid-ProofVault/` (your canonical eblets), `BISHOP_DROPZONE/` (drafts under review), Knight's in-flight `release/` artifacts, and your `.claude/` memory files. An agentic IDE that scans and modifies could clobber any of those. Secrets exposure alone is a hard "no."

2. **Knight is mid-build on the same tree** (v0.1.27-full SCOPE 6, gemma4:12b bundle). Two agentic actors on the same file system = race conditions and lost edits.

3. **Uncommitted work on disk right now**: SEG-K pre-staged Hugo edits + SEG-L changelog entry are sitting unstaged. If Antigravity scans + auto-modifies, those vanish.

**Safer pattern for the welcome-cohesion task you want Gemini/Antigravity on:**

```
1. Commit or stash everything first:
   cd C:\Users\Administrator\Documents\LianaBanyanPlatform
   git status
   git stash push -u -m "bp078-pre-antigravity"   (or commit)

2. Branch:
   git checkout -b welcome-cohesion-bp078

3. Open Antigravity pointing at a NARROW subfolder:
   C:\Users\Administrator\Documents\LianaBanyanPlatform\platform\src\
   (the web app only — keeps secrets, vault, memory, electron renderer out of scope)

   Even narrower if Antigravity supports it: just the 3 files in play
   - platform/src/AppShell.tsx
   - platform/src/components/CrossPortalNav.tsx
   - platform/src/pages/WelcomeV2Page.tsx
   - platform/src/components/v2/welcome/PathwayMapVisual.tsx

4. When done, merge the branch into main, Bishop verifies the diff.
```

Honest read: **mostly Titanic, partly genius.** Let me split it.

**The Titanic part:** "Pull all the parts I want into a new project" sounds clean but the existing platform has years of working surfaces — Sweet Sixteen pages, Stripe checkout, Supabase auth, Frontier mesh wiring, Cue Card sharing, Battery Dispatch, the 6-pathway routes, 16 deep-build pages, the substrate eblet pipeline. Rebuilding any one of those from scratch costs days. Rebuilding all of them costs weeks-to-months. Meanwhile Knight is actively shipping into the current tree (v0.1.27-full, mesh proof, Stripe fix). A fork means Knight's work doesn't flow into the new project — you end up maintaining two codebases or abandoning Knight's stream. Saladin's Pattern says preserve the fruit tree.

**The genius part:** Using Antigravity as a Bishop-directed READ-ONLY worker is the right instinct. Same pattern as Pawn fact-check but interactive.

**Recommended hybrid (gets the bird-kill without remaking the ship):**

1. Point Antigravity at `LianaBanyanPlatform\platform\src\` in **read-only mode** (or open it in a directory mode that doesn't allow saves to that tree — verify in the IDE settings before you trust it).
2. Bishop drafts a Foreman prompt scoping the cohesion work — chrome-light /welcome + broken Explore links + desktop→platform handoff + SKU tier UI + Gauntlet real-deltas wiring.
3. Antigravity returns a **unified proposal document** (markdown with proposed diffs, not actual file writes) into `BISHOP_DROPZONE\00_FOUNDER_REVIEW\ANTIGRAVITY_COHESION_PROPOSAL_BP078.md`.
4. Bishop SEG verifies each proposed change against the real codebase (file/line/behavior check). PASS/FAIL per item.
5. You approve. Bishop SEG (or Knight if a build is needed) applies the approved edits to the EXISTING tree, on a feature branch, on top of the current uncommitted work.

You get Antigravity's read-and-plan benefit. You keep the fruit tree. Knight's stream continues. One commit at the end, not a parallel codebase.

## 👤 user — 2026-06-08T23:40:38.315Z

This is a pure document-analysis task. No external research needed. The full evidence is inlined in the package. Reading and rendering judgment now.

Lure Thread: Independent Gaps
Gap 1 (Critical): FirstStepsView join modal is unreachable by any live user path.
The trigger flag showFirstSteps is only set inside handleOnboardChoice, which is only reached from showOnboardAsk, which is never activated in current code. A user who completes the first-run spine and is sold on the AI has no route to the $5 join screen. The lure converts but the funnel exit is sealed.

Gap 2 (Critical): Gauntlet benchmark data is entirely simulated noise.
simulateDelta() returns random floats and simulateBanyanMetric() draws from a hardcoded array. The real mesh test result (p50 16.6ms, 100pp resolution, 20/20 hash-verified) exists in run_mesh_test.py and is not wired in. A user who reaches the Gauntlet and watches the benchmark is being shown theater, not proof. This is the single biggest credibility risk in the entire package.

Gap 3 (Severe): Gauntlet is hidden from default users behind a forTechies localStorage flag with no surfacing mechanism.
The tab is invisible, and no UI element exists to enable it. The Gauntlet is the proof engine that justifies the lure. Default users never see it.

Gap 4 (Moderate): Branding mismatch on the on-disk installer.
The .exe is pinned at v0.1.16 and still carries the old "Mnemosyne" brand. The live landing page carries "MnemosyneC." A user who downloads, installs, and then sees the old name has immediate trust erosion before the first-run spine even loads.

Gap 5 (Moderate): Step 3 success screen drops the user in a void.
Green checkmark fires, then "Ask it anything" jumps to Frame with no forward signal toward the cooperative, the Gauntlet, or the $5 join. The proof moment lands and is immediately wasted. No bridge exists between "AI works" and "here is what that means for you."

Three-Option Disclosure Thread: Independent Gaps
Gap 1 (Critical): The three-option user-intent split does not exist in code anywhere.
"I need help / I want to help / I want to make money" is spec language only. No file in the codebase contains those strings. The arc depends on this branch as the mechanism that routes a converted user to the right cooperative initiative cluster. It is entirely absent.

Gap 2 (Critical): SaltFighterFirstRun is dead code but contains the only 16-initiatives grid presentation.
The active spine (Bp067FirstRunSpine) never shows the 16 initiatives. A new user who completes the current first-run has no exposure to the cooperative surface at all during onboarding. The handoff from AI proof to cooperative value has no onboarding-phase vehicle.

Gap 3 (Severe): Option C (folder path for existing Ollama model) is a dead-end.
The path is stored in state only. No IPC call follows. A technically sophisticated user who arrives with an existing model install and chooses Option C gets a broken experience with no recovery prompt.

Gap 4 (Moderate): Post-join routing drops the user into the bare app with no intent context.
FirstStepsView terminates with onClose(). Even if the modal were reachable, a new $5 member lands in the raw tab shell with no "start here based on why you joined" routing. The intent split was presumably designed to fill this gap, and its absence means even a successful join is a dead end.

Cooperative Value Thread: Independent Gaps
Gap 1 (Severe): Marks are session-only and non-persistent.
The balance is explicitly commented as test-only in InitiativeProjectsPage.tsx. Earn events for review submission and node hosting are not wired. The cooperative's primary reward signal to members is inert. A user who completes a walkthrough action expecting to earn Marks earns nothing and sees no feedback.

Gap 2 (Severe): Five of sixteen initiatives render only via the generic template with no next-step in code.
VSL, Brass Tacks, Power to the People, MSA, and Rally Group each dead-end at the generic InitiativePage. A user who reads the walkthrough for "join a lending circle" and clicks has nowhere to go. These are not labeled as "coming soon"; they appear live.

Gap 3 (Moderate): Tab 14 (LB Account, the bridge between the desktop app and cooperative membership) is not part of the first-run spine.
A new member must discover it manually. The cooperative value is structurally siloed from the install experience. The node heartbeat and Frontier mesh registration, which are the most tangible proof of cooperative participation, are invisible unless the user stumbles onto Tab 14.

Gap 4 (Moderate): BroadcastScheduleTab (Tab 16) is a wireframe storing to localStorage only.
No backend persistence, no actual send mechanism. If a member expects internal cooperative communication tools to function, this surface fails silently.

Gap 5 (Low, but architecturally meaningful): No "your substrate helped someone" notification surface exists anywhere.
The mesh sharing is protocol-level only. The cooperative value proposition includes network effects and mutual aid reinforcement. Without a feedback loop showing members their participation contributing to others, the cooperative feel degrades to a features list rather than a lived community experience.

Overall Arc Verdict
The lure holds structurally: the AI-saves-you-money proof is the right hook, the first-run spine fires the auto-test cleanly, and the GauntletModeSelect with own-data ingestion is the most coherent piece in the entire package. But the arc fragments at the exact moment it should pay off. The success screen fires, the user is convinced, and then nothing routes them forward. The join modal is unreachable, the Gauntlet that would deepen conviction is hidden, and the benchmark data it would show is simulated anyway. The cooperative surface is entirely absent from the active onboarding path because the only component that displayed the 16 initiatives is dead code. When a user does reach the cooperative side, five of sixteen initiatives dead-end and the primary reward signal (Marks) is a no-op. The cooperative does not feel like "continued colossal value" yet; it feels like a landing page behind an app. The user falls off the rails the moment Step 3 fires its green checkmark and offers nothing but "Ask it anything." Every downstream gap compounds from that one missing bridge.

The One Fix First
Wire showOnboardAsk to fire immediately after the Step 3 success screen "Ask it anything" click.

This single connection restores the broken join path, creates the natural bridge between "AI proof worked" and "here is the cooperative that built it," and makes FirstStepsView reachable for the first time by any live user. Every other gap downstream of the join funnel (post-join routing, intent split, initiative surfacing) becomes patchable in sequence once a user can actually reach the $5 join screen. The Gauntlet simulation and Marks persistence are important, but a user who never reaches the join modal never becomes a member. Fix the funnel exit before fixing what lies beyond it. 


I want to give this to ROOK to architect, and then hand to you to Orchestrate - thoughts?

Good. I have sufficient research findings across all five claims. Let me now compile the verdicts.

BP078 Prov-22 Novelty Assessment: Five Verdicts
Claim A -- Staggered Swarm Data Mining with Distributed Substrate Traffic Sign Compounding
Verdict: PARTIALLY-ANTICIPATED

Closest prior art: US6708163B1 (Kargupta et al., "Collective data mining from a distributed, vertically partitioned feature space," granted 2004) and WO2007124616A1 / US8126911B2 (Intel/Hu & Lai, "Content-Based Partitioning and Mining," 2007) both disclose distributing disjoint corpus subsets across multiple compute nodes in parallel, with per-node processing and subsequent query resolution. US8122032B2 (Google, granted 2012) covers per-document identifier tagging during mining and cross-document resolution.

What remains novel: No located prior art combines the specific plow/test phase separation with a compounding "traffic sign" routing layer that encodes and distributes directional knowledge pointers (rather than raw data) for sub-second cross-mesh resolution without re-mining. The anti-popularity filter in Dependent Claim 2 preventing stale-intelligence compounding is also unlocated in prior art. Narrow independent claim language to lean hard on the traffic-sign compounding mechanism and the plow/test phase split as the distinct operative combination.

Claim B -- Bundled Local-LLM Installer with Dynamic Four-Tier Provisioning
Verdict: PARTIALLY-ANTICIPATED

Closest prior art: US20090276770A1 (IBM, automated packaging/provisioning of J2EE modules to Eclipse-based rich clients, 2009) discloses automated bundling of runtime dependencies into a rich-client installer with versioned components, closely mirroring the extraResources pattern. US20090276755A1 (IBM, OSGi dynamic bundle generation at runtime, 2009) covers dynamic runtime environment detection and bundle activation within an application framework.

What remains novel: Neither prior art combines a consumer-facing four-footprint tier-selection UI with in-process LLM model weight bundling into a single unified binary installer that auto-detects and upgrades a pre-existing local inference runtime (Ollama-class). The user-abstraction of the entire LLM infrastructure stack within a tiered Electron installer is the protectable delta. Tighten Dependent Claim 2 to explicitly recite the model-weight packaging path and runtime invocation command to satisfy enablement, as flagged in the open questions.

Bishop follow-up (B): Pearl IDs are missing for Candidates 4 and 5. Append before counsel review.

Claim C -- Staggered Swarm ThreadPool Orchestration with Automated Stop-The-Line Cascading Failure Prevention
Verdict: PARTIALLY-ANTICIPATED -- NOT a double-count vs. Prov-21; claim is distinguishable but requires tightening

Prov-21 double-count resolution: The Prov-21 canons cited (canon_bp077_six_sigma_stop_the_line_andon_cord and canon_bp077_per_domain_isolation_parallel_waves) predate BP078 and disclose the conceptual Andon cord abort and per-domain isolation tracks. However, the BP077 canons cover those mechanisms at the architectural/design level, whereas Claim C's independent claim language adds the specific operative combination of: (1) a pre-flight hardness scorer routing to tiered ThreadPoolExecutors, (2) staggered dispatch schedule within isolated domain tracks, and (3) immediate halt on first batch failure. That three-way combination is not fully recited in BP077's filed claims. Claim C is not a double-count provided the independent claim language stays anchored to the hardness-scorer-to-tiered-pool routing step. If you strip that element, the remainder collapses into BP077 and becomes a double-count. Do not strip it.

External prior art: The microservice circuit-breaker pattern is well-established in public art. US12353270B2 (Walmart, adaptive circuit breaker for cascading service failure, filed 2023) discloses a circuit breaker that trips and halts calls when a failure rate threshold is exceeded. That patent covers threshold-based trip-and-halt, not first-failure-immediate-halt. The "stop on very first batch failure" (zero-tolerance Andon cord) is meaningfully stronger than a threshold-based circuit breaker and is not anticipated. Dependent Claims 1 and 2 (async three-tier scaling; parallel waves converging to confirmation batch) add further differentiation not found in Walmart's art.

Claim D -- Structural Truth-Always Orchestration Protocol with Embedded Wake-Up Verification
Verdict: PARTIALLY-ANTICIPATED

Closest prior art: US12556493B2 / US20250358240A1 (Bhat & Myers, "Encrypted Autonomous Agent Verification in Multi-Tiered Distributed Systems," granted Feb 2026) directly cover an auditing AI agent that generates a reference value from a data structure defining operative boundaries, transmits it to multi-agent storage, and verifies worker output by comparing observed vs. reference values. This is close in structure to Claim D's adversarial-verify mechanism and boundary conditions enforcement.

What remains novel: The Bhat/Myers cluster focuses on cryptographic hash-based verification across distributed third-party agent networks. Claim D's protectable delta is the paste-ready unified dispatch artifact as the singular state-transfer mechanism -- the notion that the entire context (task, boundary conditions, return path, unpin trigger) is embedded into a single artifact that is also the wake-up mechanism. That self-contained, paste-deliverable dispatch packaging is not present in Bhat/Myers, which separates task dispatch from verification. Narrow to keep the dispatch artifact construction and embedding step as the load-bearing independent claim element.

Bishop follow-up (D): Pearl IDs are missing for Candidates 9 and 11. Append before counsel review.

Claim E -- Four-Renderer-Tree Application Taxonomy for Distinct Subsystem Isolation
Verdict: NOVEL

No located prior art anticipates the specific architecture of four strictly isolated renderer trees within a single desktop application for the purpose of separating (1) main desktop UI logic, (2) an embedded web platform context, (3) a proofing interface, and (4) a design feedback overlay, each with independent lifecycle. Multi-layer UI architectures are broadly known (Meta's layer-tree treatment per US9274766B2; NVIDIA's multi-scene renderer propagation per US9367889B2 ), but these cover rendering pipelines for multi-user/multi-scene cloud environments, not functionally-isolated subsystem renderer trees in a single-user desktop client. The functional specificity of four semantically distinct renderer trees with hard ownership/lifecycle boundaries in a single Electron-class desktop application is novel.

Claim E's priority classification as LOW is reasonable given the narrowness of the architecture, but the claim is clean. Maintain and protect.
